         <td>$8,570<sup id="cite_ref-imf_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-9">[7]</a></sup></td>
        </tr>

      <p><b>Nauru</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">nah-<span style="font-size:90%">OO</span>-roo</i></a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">NOW</span>-roo</i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_language" title="Nauruan language">Nauruan</a>: <i lang="na">Naoero</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Nauru</b> (<a href="/wiki/Nauruan_language" title="Nauruan language">Nauruan</a>: <i lang="na">Repubrikin Naoero</i>) and formerly known as <b>Pleasant Island</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microstate" title="Microstate">microstate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Central Pacific</a>. Its nearest neighbour is <a href="/wiki/Banaba_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Banaba Island">Banaba Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, 300&nbsp;km (190&nbsp;mi) to the east. It further lies northwest of <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, 1,300&nbsp;km (810&nbsp;mi) northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a> and south of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>. With only a 21&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (8.1&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) area, Nauru is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">third-smallest country in the world</a> behind <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, making it the smallest <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. Additionally, its population of 10,670 is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">the world's second smallest</a>, after Vatican City. </p>
      <p>Settled by people from <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a> <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1000 BC</span>, Nauru was <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexed</a> and claimed as a colony by the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in the late 19th century. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War&nbsp;I</a>, Nauru became a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> administered by Australia, New Zealand, and the United Kingdom. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&nbsp;II</a>, Nauru was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> troops, and was <a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)" title="Leapfrogging (strategy)">bypassed</a> by the Allied advance across the Pacific. After the war ended, the country entered into <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_trust_territories" title="United Nations trust territories">United Nations trusteeship</a>. Nauru gained its independence in 1968, and became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a> (SPC) in 1969. </p>
      <p>Nauru is a <a href="/wiki/Phosphorite" title="Phosphorite">phosphate-rock</a> island with rich deposits near the surface, which allowed easy <a href="/wiki/Surface_mining" title="Surface mining">strip mining</a> operations. Its remaining phosphate resources are not economically viable for extraction.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> When the phosphate reserves were exhausted, and the island's environment had been seriously harmed by mining, the trust that had been established to manage the island's wealth diminished in value. To earn income, Nauru briefly became a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> and illegal <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> centre.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> From 2001 to 2008, and again from 2012, it accepted aid from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Australia">Australian Government</a> in exchange for hosting the <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Regional_Processing_Centre" title="Nauru Regional Processing Centre">Nauru Regional Processing Centre</a>, a controversial <a href="/wiki/Australian_immigration_detention_facilities" title="Australian immigration detention facilities">offshore Australian immigration detention facility</a>. As a result of heavy dependence on Australia, some sources have identified Nauru as a <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client state</a> of Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> The sovereign state is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African,_Caribbean,_and_Pacific_Group_of_States" class="mw-redirect" title="African, Caribbean, and Pacific Group of States">African, Caribbean, and Pacific Group of States</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nauru" title="History of Nauru">History of Nauru</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">British Western Pacific Territories</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauruan-warrior-1880ers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Nauruan-warrior-1880ers.jpg/170px-Nauruan-warrior-1880ers.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/Nauruan-warrior-1880ers.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauruan-warrior-1880ers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Photo of a Nauruan warrior during the <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_Civil_War" title="Nauruan Civil War">Nauruan Civil War</a> around 1880
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nauru was first inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesians</a> at least 3,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-UNCCD_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNCCD-19">[17]</a></sup> There were traditionally 12 clans or tribes on Nauru, which are represented in the twelve-pointed star on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Nauru" title="Flag of Nauru">country's flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> Traditionally, Nauruans traced their descent <a href="/wiki/Matrilineality" title="Matrilineality">matrilineally</a>. Inhabitants practised <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>: they caught juvenile <a href="/wiki/Milkfish" title="Milkfish"><i>ibija</i> fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acclimatization" title="Acclimatization">acclimatised</a> them to freshwater, and raised them in the <a href="/wiki/Buada_Lagoon" title="Buada Lagoon">Buada Lagoon</a>, providing a reliable food source. The other locally grown components of their diet included <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pandanus_tectorius" title="Pandanus tectorius">pandanus fruit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pollock_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pollock-21">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spennemann_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spennemann-22">[20]</a></sup> The name "Nauru" may derive from the <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_language" title="Nauruan language">Nauruan</a> word <i><i lang="na" title="Nauruan-language text">Anáoero</i></i>, which means 'I go to the beach.'<sup id="cite_ref-west_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-west-23">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1798, the British sea captain <a href="/wiki/John_Fearn_(whaler)" title="John Fearn (whaler)">John Fearn</a>, on his trading ship <i>Hunter</i> (300 tons), became the first Westerner to report sighting Nauru, calling it "Pleasant Island", because of its attractive appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-WM1985_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WM1985-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ellis_1935_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis_1935-25">[23]</a></sup> From at least 1826, Nauruans had regular contact with Europeans on whaling and trading ships who called for provisions and fresh drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> The last whaler to call during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_sail" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of sail">age of sail</a> visited in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Around this time, deserters from European ships began to live on the island. The islanders traded food for alcoholic <a href="/wiki/Palm_wine" title="Palm wine">palm wine</a> and firearms.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> The firearms were used during the 10-year <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_Civil_War" title="Nauruan Civil War">Nauruan Civil War</a> that began in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-German_Declarations_about_the_Western_Pacific_Ocean" title="Anglo-German Declarations about the Western Pacific Ocean">agreement with Great Britain</a>, Nauru was annexed by Germany in 1888 and incorporated into Germany's <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> Protectorate for administrative purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-firth_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firth-31">[29]</a></sup> The arrival of the Germans ended the civil war, and kings were established as rulers of the island. The most widely known of these was King <a href="/wiki/Aweida" title="Aweida">Auweyida</a>. Christian missionaries from the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> arrived in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-hill_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hill-32">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> The German settlers called the island "Nawodo" or "Onawero".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> The Germans ruled Nauru for almost three decades. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rasch" title="Robert Rasch">Robert Rasch</a>, a German trader who married a Nauruan woman, was the first administrator, appointed in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-hill_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hill-32">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">Phosphate</a> was discovered on Nauru in 1900 by the prospector <a href="/wiki/Albert_Fuller_Ellis" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert Fuller Ellis">Albert Fuller Ellis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-firth_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firth-31">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ellis_1935_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis_1935-25">[23]</a></sup> The Pacific Phosphate Company began to exploit the reserves in 1906 by agreement with Germany, exporting its first shipment in 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-WM1985_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WM1985-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-35">[33]</a></sup> In 1914, following the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Nauru was captured by Australian troops. In 1919 it was agreed by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied and Associated Powers</a> that <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">His Britannic Majesty</a> should be the administering authority under a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a>. The Nauru Island Agreement forged in 1919 between the governments of the United Kingdom, Australia, and New Zealand provided for the administration of the island and extraction of the phosphate deposits by an intergovernmental <a href="/wiki/British_Phosphate_Commission" title="British Phosphate Commission">British Phosphate Commission</a> (BPC).<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gowdy_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gowdy-36">[34]</a></sup> The terms of the League of Nations mandate were drawn up in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cmd._1202_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cmd._1202-37">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The island experienced an <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a> <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemic</a> in 1920, with a mortality rate of 18 per cent among native Nauruans.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1923, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> gave Australia a trustee mandate over Nauru, with the United Kingdom and New Zealand as co-trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> On 6&nbsp;and 7 December 1940, the German auxiliary cruisers <i><a href="/wiki/German_auxiliary_cruiser_Komet" title="German auxiliary cruiser Komet">Komet</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/German_auxiliary_cruiser_Orion" title="German auxiliary cruiser Orion">Orion</a></i> <a href="/wiki/German_attacks_on_Nauru" title="German attacks on Nauru">sank five supply ships</a> in the vicinity of Nauru. <i>Komet</i> then shelled Nauru's phosphate mining areas, oil storage depots, and the shiploading cantilever.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bogart_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bogart-41">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg/220px-Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg/330px-Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg/440px-Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_Island_under_attack_by_Liberator_bombers_of_the_Seventh_Air_Force..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/US_Army_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army Air Force">US Army Air Force</a> bombing the Japanese airstrip on Nauru, 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-PacMag_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PacMag-42">[40]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> troops <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Nauru" title="Japanese occupation of Nauru">occupied Nauru</a> on 25 August 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-bogart_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bogart-41">[39]</a></sup> The Japanese built an airfield which was bombed for the first time on 25 March 1943, preventing food supplies from being flown to Nauru. The Japanese deported 1,200 Nauruans to work as labourers in the <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Chuuk Islands">Chuuk Islands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PacMag_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PacMag-42">[40]</a></sup> which was also occupied by Japan. As part of the Allied strategy of <a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)" title="Leapfrogging (strategy)">island hopping</a> from the Pacific islands towards the main islands of Japan, Nauru was bypassed and left to "wither on the vine". Nauru was finally liberated on 13 September 1945, when commander Hisayaki Soeda surrendered the island to the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Army" title="Australian Army">Australian Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> The surrender was accepted by <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">Brigadier</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Rowlstone_Stevenson" title="John Rowlstone Stevenson">J. R. Stevenson</a>, who represented <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_general_(Australia)" title="Lieutenant general (Australia)">Lieutenant General</a> <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Sturdee" title="Vernon Sturdee">Vernon Sturdee</a>, the commander of the First Australian Army, aboard the warship <a href="/wiki/HMAS_Diamantina_(K377)" title="HMAS Diamantina (K377)">HMAS <i>Diamantina</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> Arrangements were made to repatriate from Chuuk the 737&nbsp;Nauruans who survived Japanese captivity there. They were returned to Nauru by the BPC ship <i>Trienza</i> in January 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1947, a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_trust_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations trust territory">trusteeship</a> was established by the United Nations, with Australia, New Zealand, and the United Kingdom as trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-highet_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highet-47">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> Under those arrangements, the UK, Australia, and New Zealand were a joint administering authority. The Nauru Island Agreement provided for the first administrator to be appointed by Australia for five years, leaving subsequent appointments to be decided by the three governments.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cmd._1202_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cmd._1202-37">[35]</a></sup> However, in practice, administrative power was exercised by Australia alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenneth_Roberts-Wray_1966._P._884-30">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cmd._1202_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cmd._1202-37">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1948, Chinese guano mining workers went on strike over pay and conditions. The Australian administration imposed a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> with <a href="/wiki/Native_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Police">Native Police</a> and armed volunteers of locals and Australian officials being mobilised. This force, using sub-machine guns and other firearms, opened fire on the Chinese workers killing two and wounding sixteen. Around 50 of the workers were arrested and two of these were bayoneted to death while in custody. The trooper who bayoneted the prisoners was charged but later acquitted on grounds that the wounds were "accidentally received."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> The governments of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> made official complaints against <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> over this incident.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1964, it was proposed to relocate the population of Nauru to <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Island_(Queensland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Curtis Island (Queensland)">Curtis Island</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, Australia. By that time, Nauru had been extensively mined for phosphate by companies from Australia, Britain and New Zealand damaging the landscape so much that it was thought the island would be uninhabitable by the 1990s. Rehabilitating the island was seen as financially impossible. In 1962, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Australian Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Menzies" title="Robert Menzies">Robert Menzies</a>, said that the three countries involved in the mining had an obligation to provide a solution for the Nauruan people, and proposed finding a new island for them. In 1963, the Australian Government proposed to acquire all the land on Curtis Island (which was considerably larger than Nauru) and then offer the Nauruans freehold title over the island and that the Nauruans would become Australian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> The cost of resettling the Nauruans on Curtis Island was estimated to be <a href="/wiki/Australian_pound" title="Australian pound">£</a>10&nbsp;million, which included housing and infrastructure and the establishment of pastoral, agricultural, and fishing industries.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> However, the Nauruan people did not wish to become Australian citizens and wanted to be given sovereignty over Curtis Island to establish themselves as an independent nation, which Australia would not agree to.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> Nauru rejected the proposal to move to Curtis Island, instead choosing to become an independent nation operating their mines in Nauru.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru became self-governing in January 1966, and following a two-year constitutional convention, it became independent on 31 January 1968 under founding president <a href="/wiki/Hammer_DeRoburt" title="Hammer DeRoburt">Hammer DeRoburt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-davidson_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davidson-57">[55]</a></sup> In 1967, the people of Nauru purchased the assets of the British Phosphate Commissioners, and in June 1970 control passed to the locally owned <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Phosphate_Corporation" title="Nauru Phosphate Corporation">Nauru Phosphate Corporation</a> (NPC).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-35">[33]</a></sup> Income from the mines made Nauruans among the richest people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KN-20180916_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KN-20180916-59">[57]</a></sup> In 1989, Nauru took legal action against Australia in the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> over Australia's administration of the island, in particular, Australia's failure to remedy the environmental damage caused by phosphate mining. <i>Certain Phosphate Lands: Nauru v.&nbsp;Australia</i> led to an out-of-court settlement to rehabilitate the mined-out areas of Nauru.<sup id="cite_ref-highet_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highet-47">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nauru" title="Geography of Nauru">Geography of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-map.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Nauru-map.gif/220px-Nauru-map.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Nauru-map.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="355"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-map.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Nauru
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nauru is a 21&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (8.1&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> oval-shaped island in the southwestern Pacific Ocean, 55.95&nbsp;km (34.77&nbsp;mi) south of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> The island is surrounded by a coral reef, which is exposed at low tide and dotted with pinnacles.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> The presence of the reef has prevented the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">seaport</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Canals_in_Nauru" title="Canals in Nauru">channels</a> in the reef allow small boats access to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> A fertile coastal strip 150 to 300&nbsp;m (490 to 980&nbsp;ft) wide lies inland from the beach.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Coral cliffs surround Nauru's central plateau. The highest point of the plateau, called the <a href="/wiki/Command_Ridge" title="Command Ridge">Command Ridge</a>, is 71&nbsp;m (233&nbsp;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The only fertile areas on Nauru are on the narrow coastal belt where <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a> palms flourish. The land around <a href="/wiki/Buada_Lagoon" title="Buada Lagoon">Buada Lagoon</a> supports bananas, <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a>, vegetables, <a href="/wiki/Pandanus_tectorius" title="Pandanus tectorius">pandanus trees</a>, and indigenous hardwoods, such as the <a href="/wiki/Calophyllum_inophyllum" title="Calophyllum inophyllum">tamanu tree</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru was one of three great <a href="/wiki/Phosphorite" title="Phosphorite">phosphate rock</a> islands in the Pacific Ocean, along with <a href="/wiki/Banaba_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Banaba Island">Banaba</a> (Ocean Island), in <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Makatea" title="Makatea">Makatea</a>, in <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>. The phosphate reserves on Nauru are now almost entirely depleted. Phosphate mining in the central plateau has left a barren terrain of jagged limestone pinnacles up to 15&nbsp;m (49&nbsp;ft) high. Mining has stripped and devastated about 80 per cent of Nauru's land area, leaving it uninhabitable,<sup id="cite_ref-KN-20180916_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KN-20180916-59">[57]</a></sup> and has also affected the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a>; 40 per cent of marine life is estimated to have been killed by silt and phosphate runoff.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNCCC_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNCCC-64">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are limited natural sources of freshwater on Nauru. Rooftop <a href="/wiki/Rainwater_tank" title="Rainwater tank">storage tanks</a> collect rainwater. The islanders are mostly dependent on three <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a> plants housed at Nauru's Utilities Agency. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Nauru's climate is hot and very humid year-round because of its proximity to the equator and the ocean. Nauru is hit by <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> rains between November and February, but rarely has cyclones. Annual rainfall is highly variable and is influenced by the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o%E2%80%93Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño–Southern Oscillation">El Niño–Southern Oscillation</a>, with several significant recorded droughts.<sup id="cite_ref-UNCCD_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNCCD-19">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> The temperature on Nauru ranges between 30 and 35&nbsp;°C (86 and 95&nbsp;°F) during the day and is quite stable at around 25&nbsp;°C (77&nbsp;°F) at night.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Streams and rivers do not exist in Nauru. Water is gathered from roof catchment systems. Water is brought to Nauru as ballast on ships returning for loads of phosphate.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Fauna is sparse on the island because of a lack of vegetation and the consequences of phosphates mining. Many indigenous birds have disappeared or become rare owing to the destruction of their habitat.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> There are about 60&nbsp;recorded <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species native to the island, none of which are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>. <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">Coconut</a> farming, mining, and introduced species have seriously disturbed the native vegetation.<sup id="cite_ref-UNCCD_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNCCD-19">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are no native land <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a>, but there are native <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>, land crabs, and birds, including the endemic <a href="/wiki/Nauru_reed_warbler" title="Nauru reed warbler">Nauru reed warbler</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_rat" title="Polynesian rat">Polynesian rat</a>, cats, dogs, pigs, and chickens have been introduced to Nauru from ships.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> The diversity of the reef marine life makes fishing a popular activity for tourists on the island; also popular are <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkelling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Nauru" title="Politics of Nauru">Politics of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-parliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nauru-parliament.jpg/220px-Nauru-parliament.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nauru-parliament.jpg/330px-Nauru-parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nauru-parliament.jpg/440px-Nauru-parliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="459"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-parliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Parliament of Nauru
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The president of Nauru is <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Aingimea" title="Lionel Aingimea">Lionel Aingimea</a>, who heads a 19-member <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliament. The country is a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>. Nauru also participates in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>. Recently Nauru became a member country of the <a href="/wiki/International_Renewable_Energy_Agency" title="International Renewable Energy Agency">International Renewable Energy Agency</a> (IRENA). The Republic of Nauru became the 189th member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in April 2016. </p>
      <p>Nauru is a republic with a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government.<sup id="cite_ref-davidson_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-davidson-57">[55]</a></sup> The president is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and is dependent on parliamentary confidence to remain president. A 19-member unicameral parliament is elected every three years.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> The parliament elects the president from its members, and the president appoints a cabinet of five to six members.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru does not have any formal structure for political parties, and candidates typically stand for office as independents; fifteen of the 19&nbsp;members of the current Parliament are independents. Four parties that have been active in Nauruan politics are the Nauru Party, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Nauru" title="Democratic Party of Nauru">Democratic Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru_First" title="Nauru First">Nauru First</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Nauru)" title="Centre Party (Nauru)">Centre Party</a>. However, alliances within the government are often formed based on extended family ties rather than party affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 1992 to 1999, Nauru had a local government system known as the Nauru Island Council (NIC). This nine-member council was designed to provide municipal services. The NIC was dissolved in 1999 and all assets and liabilities became vested in the national government.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Land_tenure" title="Land tenure">Land tenure</a> on Nauru is unusual: all Nauruans have certain rights to all land on the island, which is owned by individuals and family groups. Government and corporate entities do not own any land, and they must enter into a lease arrangement with landowners to use land. Non-Nauruans cannot own land on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-UNCCD_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNCCD-19">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru had 17&nbsp;changes of administration between 1989 and 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-75">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Dowiyogo" title="Bernard Dowiyogo">Bernard Dowiyogo</a> died in office in March 2003 and <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Scotty" title="Ludwig Scotty">Ludwig Scotty</a> was elected as the president, later being re-elected to serve a full term in October 2004. Following a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">vote of no confidence</a> on 19 December 2007, Scotty was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Stephen" title="Marcus Stephen">Marcus Stephen</a>. Stephen resigned in November 2011, and <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Pitcher" title="Freddie Pitcher">Freddie Pitcher</a> became president. <a href="/wiki/Sprent_Dabwido" title="Sprent Dabwido">Sprent Dabwido</a> then filed a motion of no confidence in Pitcher, resulting in him becoming president.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/2013_Nauruan_parliamentary_election" title="2013 Nauruan parliamentary election">parliamentary elections in 2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baron_Waqa" title="Baron Waqa">Baron Waqa</a> was elected president. </p>
      <p>Its <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Nauru" title="Supreme Court of Nauru">Supreme Court</a>, headed by the Chief Justice, is paramount on <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Nauru" title="Constitution of Nauru">constitutional issues</a>. Other cases can be appealed to the two-judge Appellate Court. Parliament cannot overturn court decisions. Historically, Appellate Court rulings could be appealed to the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia" title="High Court of Australia">High Court of Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> though this happened only rarely and the Australian court's appellate jurisdiction ended entirely on 12 March 2018 after the Government of Nauru unilaterally ended the arrangement.<sup id="cite_ref-Gans_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gans-80">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-81">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-82">[80]</a></sup> Lower courts consist of the District Court and the Family Court, both of which are headed by a Resident Magistrate, who also is the Registrar of the Supreme Court. There are two other quasi-courts: the Public Service Appeal Board and the Police Appeal Board, both of which are presided over by the Chief Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Nauru" title="Foreign relations of Nauru">Foreign relations of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Following independence in 1968, Nauru joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> as a Special Member; it became a full member in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-83">[81]</a></sup> The country was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> in 1991 and the United Nations in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> Nauru is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a>, the South Pacific Regional Environment Programme, the South Pacific Commission, and the South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> The US <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_Radiation_Measurement_Climate_Research_Facility" title="Atmospheric Radiation Measurement Climate Research Facility">Atmospheric Radiation Measurement</a> program operates a climate-monitoring facility on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg/220px-Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg/330px-Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg/440px-Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1072" data-file-height="712"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_cadet_police_on_training_exercise_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nauruan police cadets undergoing training. Nauru <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_armed_forces" title="List of countries without armed forces">has no armed forces</a>, though there is a small police force under civilian control.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nauru <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_armed_forces" title="List of countries without armed forces">has no armed forces</a>, though there is a small police force under civilian control.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> Australia is responsible for Nauru's defence under an informal agreement between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> The September 2005 <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">memorandum of understanding</a> between Australia and Nauru provides the latter with financial aid and technical assistance, including a Secretary of Finance to prepare the budget, and advisers on health and education. This aid is in return for Nauru's housing of asylum seekers while their applications for entry into Australia are processed.<sup id="cite_ref-DFAT_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFAT-75">[73]</a></sup> Nauru uses the <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">Australian dollar</a> as its official currency.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru has used its position as a member of the United Nations to gain financial support from both <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (officially the Republic of China or ROC) and mainland China (officially the People's Republic of China or PRC) by changing its recognition from one to the other under the <a href="/wiki/One-China_policy" title="One-China policy">One-China policy</a>. On 21 July 2002, Nauru signed an agreement to establish diplomatic relations with the PRC, accepting US$130&nbsp;million from the PRC for this action.<sup id="cite_ref-harding_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harding-87">[85]</a></sup> In response, the ROC severed diplomatic relations with Nauru two days later. Nauru later re-established links with the ROC on 14 May 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> and diplomatic ties with the PRC were officially severed on 31 May 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> However, the PRC continues to maintain a representative office on Nauru.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Nauru recognised <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> as an independent country, and in 2009 Nauru became the fourth country, after Russia, Nicaragua, and Venezuela, to recognise <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>, a breakaway region of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>. Russia was reported to be giving Nauru US$50&nbsp;million in humanitarian aid as a result of this recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-harding_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harding-87">[85]</a></sup> On 15 July 2008, the Nauruan government announced a port refurbishment programme, financed with US$9&nbsp;million of development aid received from Russia. The Nauru government claims this aid is not related to its recognising Abkhazia and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

2x" data-file-width="5250" data-file-height="3750"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:03.07_%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%9C%83%E6%99%A4%E8%AB%BE%E9%AD%AF%E5%85%B1%E5%92%8C%E5%9C%8B%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E7%93%A6%E5%8D%A1%EF%BC%88Baron_Divavesi_Waqa%EF%BC%89%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%BE%86%E8%A8%AA%E4%BB%A3%E8%A1%A8%E5%9C%98%EF%BC%8C%E4%B8%A6%E7%9B%B8%E4%BA%92%E8%B4%88%E7%A6%AE_(33170018521).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former Nauru President <a href="/wiki/Baron_Waqa" title="Baron Waqa">Baron Waqa</a> and Taiwanese President <a href="/wiki/Tsai_Ing-wen" title="Tsai Ing-wen">Tsai Ing-wen</a> in Taiwan, 7 March 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A significant portion of Nauru's income has been in the form of aid from Australia. In 2001, the <a href="/wiki/MV_Tampa" title="MV Tampa">MV <i>Tampa</i></a>, a Norwegian ship that had rescued 438&nbsp;refugees from a stranded 20-metre-long boat, was seeking to dock in Australia. In what became known as <a href="/wiki/Tampa_affair" title="Tampa affair">the <i>Tampa</i> affair</a>, the ship was refused entry and boarded by Australian troops. The refugees were eventually loaded onto Royal Australian Navy vessel HMAS <i>Manoora</i> and taken to Nauru to be held in detention facilities which later became part of the Howard government's <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Solution" title="Pacific Solution">Pacific Solution</a>. Nauru operated two <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Regional_Processing_Centre" title="Nauru Regional Processing Centre">detention centres known as State House and Topside</a> for these refugees in exchange for Australian aid.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> By November 2005, only two refugees, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Sagar" title="Mohammed Sagar">Mohammed Sagar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Faisal" title="Muhammad Faisal">Muhammad Faisal</a> remained on Nauru from those first sent there in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-TheAge_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAge-93">[91]</a></sup> with Sagar finally resettling in early 2007. The Australian government sent further groups of asylum-seekers to Nauru in late 2006 and early 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> The refugee centre was closed in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> but, following the Australian government's re-adoption of the Pacific Solution in August 2012, it has re-opened it.<sup id="cite_ref-SBS_World_News_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBS_World_News-95">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2017, at the 34th regular session of the UN Human Rights Council, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> made a joint statement on behalf of Nauru and some other Pacific nations raising human rights violations in <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a>, which has been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> since 1963,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> and requested that the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights produce a report.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-98">[96]</a></sup> Indonesia rejected the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-SBSMar17_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBSMar17-98">[96]</a></sup> More than 100,000 Papuans have died during a 50-year <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Amnesty International has since described the conditions of the refugees of war living in Nauru as a "horror",<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> with reports of children as young as eight attempting suicide and engaging in acts of self-harm.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-102">[100]</a></sup> In 2018, the situation gained attention as a "mental health crisis", with an estimated thirty children suffering from traumatic withdrawal syndrome, also known as <a href="/wiki/Resignation_syndrome" title="Resignation syndrome">resignation syndrome</a>. The condition is a deteriorating psychiatric condition wherein the sufferer can eventually become unresponsive and their body can begin to shut down. This condition has also been observed in other groups of asylum seekers.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-102">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_in_Nauru" title="List of settlements in Nauru">List of settlements in Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-districts-fr.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nauru-districts-fr.svg/290px-Nauru-districts-fr.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nauru-districts-fr.svg/435px-Nauru-districts-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nauru-districts-fr.svg/580px-Nauru-districts-fr.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="488"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru-districts-fr.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Nauru showing its districts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nauru is divided into fourteen administrative districts, which are grouped into <a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Nauru" title="Constituencies of Nauru">eight electoral constituencies</a> and are further divided into villages.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> The most populous district is Denigomodu, with 1,804 residents, of which 1,497 reside in an <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Phosphate_Corporation" title="Nauru Phosphate Corporation">NPC</a> settlement called "Location". The following table shows population by district according to the 2011 census.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> </p>
