      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Nauru" title="Economy of Nauru">Economy of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_satellite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nauru_satellite.jpg/220px-Nauru_satellite.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nauru_satellite.jpg/330px-Nauru_satellite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nauru_satellite.jpg/440px-Nauru_satellite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1021" data-file-height="1125"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru_satellite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A satellite image of Nauru, 2002
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Nauruan economy peaked in the mid-1970s, when its <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> per capita was estimated to be US$50,000, second only to Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-KN-20180916_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KN-20180916-59">[57]</a></sup> Most of this came from phosphate mining, which declined from the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-CER-NAU-2007_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CER-NAU-2007-105">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup> There are few other resources, and most necessities are imported.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> Small-scale mining is still conducted by RONPhos, formerly known as the <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Phosphate_Corporation" title="Nauru Phosphate Corporation">Nauru Phosphate Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> The government places a percentage of RONPhos's earnings into the <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Phosphate_Royalties_Trust" title="Nauru Phosphate Royalties Trust">Nauru Phosphate Royalties Trust</a>. The trust manages long-term investments, which were intended to support the citizens after the phosphate reserves were exhausted.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of mismanagement, the trust's fixed and <a href="/wiki/Current_asset" title="Current asset">current assets</a> were reduced considerably and may never fully recover. The failed investments included financing <i><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_the_Musical:_A_Portrait_of_Love" title="Leonardo the Musical: A Portrait of Love">Leonardo the Musical</a></i> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-mellow_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mellow-108">[106]</a></sup> The Mercure Hotel in Sydney<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nauru_House" title="Nauru House">Nauru House</a> in Melbourne were sold in 2004 to finance debts and <a href="/wiki/Air_Nauru" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Nauru">Air Nauru</a>'s only <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing&nbsp;737</a> was repossessed in December 2005. Normal air service resumed after the aircraft was replaced with a Boeing 737-300 airliner in June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> In 2005, the corporation sold its remaining real estate in Melbourne, the vacant Savoy Tavern site, for $7.5&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The value of the trust is estimated to have shrunk from <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">A$</a>1.3&nbsp;billion in 1991 to A$138&nbsp;million in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-ADB_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADB-112">[110]</a></sup> Nauru currently lacks money to perform many of the basic functions of government; for example, the National Bank of Nauru is insolvent. The CIA World Factbook estimated a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP per capita</a> of US$5,000 in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> 2007 economic report on Nauru estimated GDP per capita at US$2,400 to US$2,715.<sup id="cite_ref-CER-NAU-2007_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CER-NAU-2007-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are no personal taxes in Nauru. The unemployment rate is estimated to be 23 percent, and of those who have jobs, the government employs 95 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Economist_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-113">[111]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> notes that, although the administration has a strong public mandate to implement economic reforms, in the absence of an alternative to phosphate mining, the medium-term outlook is for continued dependence on external assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-ADB_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADB-112">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nauru" title="Tourism in Nauru">Tourism</a> is not a major contributor to the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-pitic_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitic-114">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru,_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_(10729889683).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg/220px-The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg/330px-The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg/440px-The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru%2C_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_%2810729889683%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_site_of_secondary_mining_of_Phosphate_rock_in_Nauru,_2007._Photo-_Lorrie_Graham_(10729889683).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">Limestone</a> pinnacles remain after phosphate mining at the site of one of Nauru's secondary mines
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1990s, Nauru became a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> and offered passports to foreign nationals for a fee.<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times-115">[113]</a></sup> The inter-governmental <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force_on_Money_Laundering" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering">Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering</a> (FATF) identified Nauru as one of 15 "<a href="/wiki/FATF_Blacklist" class="mw-redirect" title="FATF Blacklist">non-cooperative</a>" countries in its fight against <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>. During the 1990s, it was possible to establish a licensed bank in Nauru for only US$25,000 with no other requirements. Under pressure from FATF, Nauru introduced anti-avoidance legislation in 2003, after which foreign <a href="/wiki/Hot_money" title="Hot money">hot money</a> left the country. In October 2005, after satisfactory results from the legislation and its enforcement, FATF lifted the non-cooperative designation.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 2001 to 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Nauru_detention_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Nauru detention centre">Nauru detention centre</a> provided a significant source of income for the country. The Nauruan authorities reacted with concern to its closure by Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> In February 2008, the Foreign Affairs minister, Dr <a href="/wiki/Kieren_Keke" title="Kieren Keke">Kieren Keke</a>, stated that the closure would result in 100&nbsp;Nauruans losing their jobs, and would affect 10&nbsp;per cent of the island's population directly or indirectly: "We have got a huge number of families that are suddenly going to be without any income. We are looking at ways we can try and provide some welfare assistance but our capacity to do that is very limited. Literally we have got a major unemployment crisis in front of us."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> The detention centre was re-opened in August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SBS_World_News_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBS_World_News-95">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2017 the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD) upgraded its rating of Nauru's standards of tax transparency. Previously Nauru had been listed alongside fourteen other countries that had failed to show that they could comply with international tax transparency standards and regulations. The OECD subsequently put Nauru through a fast-tracked compliance process and the country was given a "largely compliant" rating.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Nauru 2017–2018 budget, delivered by Minister for Finance David Adeang, forecasted A$128.7&nbsp;million in revenues and A$128.6&nbsp;million in expenditures and projected modest economic growth for the nation over the next two years.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Nauru" title="Demographics of Nauru">Demographics of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Nauru had 10,670&nbsp;residents as of July 2018, making it the second smallest sovereign state after <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-6">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-7">[5]</a></sup> The population was previously larger, but in 2006 1,500&nbsp;people left the island during a repatriation of immigrant workers from Kiribati and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>. The repatriation was motivated by significant <a href="/wiki/Layoff" title="Layoff">layoffs</a> in phosphate mining.<sup id="cite_ref-CER-NAU-2007_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CER-NAU-2007-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Westernization" title="Westernization">Westernized</a> countries in the South Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Fifty-eight percent of people in Nauru are ethnically <a href="/wiki/Nauruans" title="Nauruans">Nauruan</a>, 26 percent are other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a>, 8 percent are <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a>, and 8 percent are <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The official language of Nauru is <a href="/wiki/Nauruan_language" title="Nauruan language">Nauruan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-directory_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-directory-1">[1]</a></sup> a distinct <a href="/wiki/Micronesian_languages" title="Micronesian languages">Micronesian</a> language, which is spoken by 96 per cent of ethnic Nauruans at home.<sup id="cite_ref-CER-NAU-2007_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CER-NAU-2007-105">[103]</a></sup> English is widely spoken and is the language of government and commerce, as Nauruan is not used outside of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-state_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Nauru" title="Religion in Nauru">Religion in Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru(09).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nauru%2809%29.jpg/220px-Nauru%2809%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nauru%2809%29.jpg/330px-Nauru%2809%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Nauru%2809%29.jpg/440px-Nauru%2809%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nauru(09).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Church in Nauru
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Nauru" title="Religion in Nauru">religion practised on the island</a> is Christianity (the main denominations are <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Congregational_Church" title="Nauru Congregational Church">Nauru Congregational Church</a> 35.71%, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> 32.96% Assemblies of God 12.98% and <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> 1.48%).<sup id="cite_ref-state_4-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> The Constitution provides for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>. The government has restricted the religious practices of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, most of whom are foreign workers employed by the government-owned Nauru Phosphate Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The Catholics are pastorally served by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Tarawa_and_Nauru" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Tarawa and Nauru">Roman Catholic Diocese of Tarawa and Nauru</a>, with see at <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> in Kiribati. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Nauru" title="Culture of Nauru">Culture of Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Angam_Day" title="Angam Day">Angam Day</a>, held on 26 October, celebrates the recovery of the Nauruan population after the two World Wars and the 1920 influenza epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> The displacement of the indigenous culture by colonial and contemporary Western influences is significant.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> Few of the old customs have been preserved, but some forms of traditional music, arts and crafts, and fishing are still practised.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are no daily news publications on Nauru, although there is one fortnightly publication, <i>Mwinen Ko</i>. There is a state-owned television station, <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Television" title="Nauru Television">Nauru Television</a> (NTV), which broadcasts programs from New Zealand and Australia, and a state-owned non-commercial radio station, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Nauru" title="Radio Nauru">Radio Nauru</a>, which carries programs from <a href="/wiki/Radio_Australia" title="Radio Australia">Radio Australia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg/220px-Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg/330px-Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="230"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Linkbelt1999-Finalspiel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a>, played at <a href="/wiki/Linkbelt_Oval" title="Linkbelt Oval">Linkbelt Oval</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> is the most popular sport in Nauru—it and weightlifting are considered the country's national sports. There is an <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football_in_Nauru" title="Australian rules football in Nauru">Australian rules football league</a> with eight teams.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> Other sports popular in Nauru include volleyball, netball, fishing, weightlifting and tennis. Many weightlifters on the islands have skilfully secured competitions and defeated athletes of far bigger nations. Nauru participates in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nauru_at_the_Olympics" title="Nauru at the Olympics">has participated in the Summer Olympic Games</a> in weightlifting and judo.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nauru_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Nauru national basketball team">Nauru's national basketball team</a> competed at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_1969_South_Pacific_Games" title="Basketball at the 1969 South Pacific Games">1969 Pacific Games</a>, where it defeated the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Solomon Islands national basketball team">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiji national basketball team">Fiji</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Nauru_national_rugby_sevens_team" title="Nauru national rugby sevens team">Nauru national rugby sevens team</a> made its international debut at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_Games" title="2015 Pacific Games">2015 Pacific Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nauru competed in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Oceania_Sevens_Championship" title="2015 Oceania Sevens Championship">2015 Oceania Sevens Championship</a> in New Zealand. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Nauru" title="Public holidays in Nauru">Public holidays in Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Independence Day is celebrated on 31 January.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Nauru" title="Education in Nauru">Education in Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">Literacy</a> on Nauru is 96&nbsp;per cent. Education is compulsory for children from six to sixteen years old, and two more non-compulsory years are offered (years 11 and 12).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> The island has three primary schools and two secondary schools, the latter being Nauru College and <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Secondary_School" title="Nauru Secondary School">Nauru Secondary School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> There is a campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a> on Nauru. Before this campus was built in 1987, students would study either by distance or abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> Since 2011, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_England_(Australia)" title="University of New England (Australia)">University of New England</a>, Australia has established a presence on the island with around 30 Nauruan teachers studying for an associate degree in education. These students will continue onto the degree to complete their studies.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> This project is led by Associate Professor Pep Serow and funded by the Australian Department of Foreign Affairs and Trade. </p>
      <p>The previous community public library was destroyed in a fire. As of 1999<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> a new one had not yet been built, and no <a href="/wiki/Bookmobile" title="Bookmobile">bookmobile</a> services are available as of that year. Sites with libraries include the University of the South Pacific campus, Nauru Secondary, Kayser College, and Aiwo Primary.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> The Nauru Community Library is in the new University of the South Pacific Nauru Campus building, which was officially opened in May 2018. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg/220px-Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg/330px-Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg/440px-Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Participants_of_a_walk_against_Diabetes_and_for_general_fitness_around_Nauru_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nauruan residents walking around <a href="/wiki/Nauru_International_Airport" title="Nauru International Airport">Nauru International Airport</a>. Nauruans are amongst the most obese people in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-TI.uk_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI.uk-136">[134]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Obesity_in_Nauru" title="Obesity in Nauru">Obesity in Nauru</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Life expectancy on Nauru in 2009 was 60.6&nbsp;years for males and 68.0&nbsp;years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-Nauru_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nauru-137">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By measure of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_body_mass_index" title="List of countries by body mass index">mean body mass index (BMI)</a>, Nauruans are the most overweight people in the world;<sup id="cite_ref-TI.uk_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI.uk-136">[134]</a></sup> 97 per cent of men and 93 per cent of women are overweight or obese.<sup id="cite_ref-TI.uk_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI.uk-136">[134]</a></sup> In 2012, the obesity rate was 71.7 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-Asahi_Shimbun_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asahi_Shimbun-138">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Obesity_in_the_Pacific" title="Obesity in the Pacific">Obesity in the Pacific islands</a> is common. </p>
      <p>Nauru has the world's highest level of <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">type 2 diabetes</a>, with more than 40 per cent of the population affected.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> Other significant dietary-related problems on Nauru include <a href="/wiki/Kidney_failure" title="Kidney failure">kidney disease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">heart disease</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nauru_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nauru-137">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg/220px-View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg/330px-View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg/440px-View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Nauru_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>View of Nauru International Airport
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The island is solely served by <a href="/wiki/Nauru_International_Airport" title="Nauru International Airport">Nauru International Airport</a>. Passenger service is provided by <a href="/wiki/Nauru_Airlines" title="Nauru Airlines">Nauru Airlines</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Air_Express" title="Pacific Air Express">Pacific Air Express</a> also providing cargo service. Flights operate five days a week to well connected airports such as <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Airport" title="Brisbane Airport">Brisbane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nadi_International_Airport" title="Nadi International Airport">Nadi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nauru does not have an official capital but Yaren is the seat of parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-directory_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-directory-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">English is not an official language, but it is widely spoken by the majority of the population and it is commonly used in government, legislation and commerce alongside Nauruan. Due to Nauru's history and relationship with Australia, <a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">Australian English</a> is the dominant variety.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-state_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-4">[3]</a></sup> And is <i>de facto</i> official.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nauru&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
